KENTUCKY UNIFORM POLICE TRAFFIC COLLISION REPORT - NARRATIVE ‘S00

[MASTER FILE # 72840588

INVESTIGATING AGENCY CAVE CITY POLICE DEPARTMENT AGENCY ORI 0050200 LOCAL CODE 2022-57392

On Saturday, [DOB-1108] at 1742 hours, | was dispatched to a collision on N Dixie Hwy.

| arrived at 1744 hours, upon arrival | observed a person wearing camouflage clothing lying on the roadway, a moped on roadway and a vehicle on the grass on the right side on the roadway.

| approached the person on the ground, Debra Marshall to check on her, Marshall advised she had injuries to her head and on the side of her body, | advised her EMS was en route.

Officer G. Avery arrived at 1744 hours, same date, and approached the operator of Unit 2, Jasmine M Reed. Avery advised she was fine and did not need medical attention but was shaken up.

Cave City Fire department arrived at 1746 hours, same date, and began first aid on Marshall. Marshall advised she was traveling southbound on Dixie Hwy when she was struck by Unit 2.

Reed advised she was traveling south on Dixie Hwy and as she approached the Travel Inn Motel she observed a moped coming out on the roadway and into her path. Reed advised she slammed on her brakes and swerved to the right in an attempt to prevent from striking her. Reed advised she was unable to move and struck Unit 1.

On Thursday, [DOB-1107] at 1737 hours, | spoke with Christina Marshall, daughter of Debra Marshall. Christina advised her mother was released from the hospital with in 24 hours and was back home.

At 2030 hours, | attempted to make contact with Debra at her residence, her husband advised she was unable to come to the door at the time due to her being asleep, | advised him | would return next day to speak to her

On Friday, 12/09/200 around 1800 hours, | made contact with Debra at her residence.

Debra advised she pulled out of the driveway and started to travel south on Dixie Hwy when she saw light getting close to her then she felt the vehicle stick her. Debra advised she when she was struck she landed on top of the hood of the vehicle then she was thrown to the ground and rolled for several feet. Debra advised she felt something struck her foot as she attempted to move out of the road way. Debra advised a female came to her and asked if she was OK. Debra advised she told the female to help her get out of the road way but the person did not assist her so she began to use her legs as she dragged herself out of the road way.

Neurological Neurological | | Normal Baseline For Patient

D: EMS unit dispatched to a vehicle vs Moped accident, moped rider not wearing a helmet R: EMS unit responded immediately with lights and sirens. Air Medical contacted to respond to TJ Samson Helipad.

A: upon arrival Cave City FD on scene had patient secured backboard with c-collar and head block. the patient stated she got hit from behind by a vehicle at unknown speed. patient also does not know if she had any loss of consciousness. patient complained of right hip pain and head pain.

A: Patient alert and oriented to person place time and event, pupils equal round reactant to light GCS 15. patient remained at GCS 15. Hematoma noted on back right of patient head with no bleeding . skin pink warm dry to touch. PMS present in extremities. upon palpation of pelvis crepitus noted. closed deformity noted on femur. puncture wound noted on right calf area bleeding controlled with kerlex. rotation present on right foot. strong pedal pulse palpated on right foot. no neurological deficits noted. ALS Assessment paramedic N.Heffron.

T: attached to monitor vitals obtained and repeated during transport. 3lead noted sinus rhythm. 18G IV established left AC saline locked. 18G IV also established in right AC. 50mcg fentanyl given IVP. Assessment performed and glucose checked. additional 50MCG fentanyl given IVP. patient stated it reduced her pain significantly.

T: patient placed on stretcher supine position, safety straps attached. transported immediately with lights and sirens to TJ Samson Helipad. upon arrival Air Evac 62 awaiting arrival, verbal report given to flight crew. patient care signed over. EMS assisted flight crew loading patient into helicopter.

HIPAA COMPLIANT MEDICAL AUTHORIZATION

(Authorization to Release Protected Health Care Information)

To: Air Evac EMS Inc — Prestonburg P.O. Box 106 West Plains, MO 65775

Dear Medical Records Clerk:

I nave retained The Whaley Law Firm, PSC to represent me in matters related to an injury sustained due toa third parties’ negligence. Please forward a copy of any & all records not previously provided to The Whaley Law Firm upon request.

Pursuant to the Health Insurance Portability & Accountability Act (HIPAA) Privacy Regulations, 45 CFR 164.508, the provider listed above is hereby authorized to release to The Whaley Law Firm, PSC or any of their representatives, all medical records, including but not limited to: Office Notes, History, Physical, Consultation Notes, Discharge Summaries, Orders, Progress Notes, Laboratory Results, Nurses’ Notes, Emergency Room Records, Operative Reports, In-Patient Records and films of X-Rays, MRIs, CT Scans, or PET Scans, Pharmacy and Drug Records, Medical Bills and Health Insurance [nformation, Medicaid/ Medicare Records, concerning ANY medical treatment that I have received from you and/or at your facility, as well as ALL such records which you keep in the regular course of business that are found in my medical record file. ,

I hereby authorize the release of ANY & ALL records regarding mental health, psychiatric (other than psychotherapy notes, which must be requested under separate authorization), Chemical Dependency or HIV.

A photostatic copy hereor shall be as valid as the original.

Thereby authorize a FREE COPY of my medical records pursuant to KRS 422.317 be sent to the extent | have not already requested my one free

copy.

The purpose of this authorization and request is to permit my attorney to obtain ALL medical information pertaining to my physical and mental condition(s). This authorization expires in three (3) years trom the date of the signature. The aforementioned expiration date has not Passed, as this matter is on-going. [ hereby authorize The Whaley Law Firm, PSC. to speak to my healthcare providers privately or to take the testimony at deposition and/or trial as may be requested.

Thave the right to revoke this authorization in writing by providing a signed, written notice of revocation to the healthcare provider listed above and to The Whaley Law Firm, PSC. | understand that there are exceptions to the right to revoke. Among the exceptions to the right to revoke are that an individual may not revoke an authorization to the extent that the covered entity has taken action in reliance thereon. Medical Providers may not condition treatment or payment on whether the above-listed patient executes this authorization. The information disclosed pursuant to

this authorization may be subject to re-disclosure and no longer protected by the privacy regulations promulgated pursuant to the Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act (HIPAA)

369.107 Legal recognition of electronic records, electronic signatures, and

(1) (2)

(3) (4)

electronic contracts.

A record or signature may not be denied legal effect or enforceability solely because it is in electronic form.

A contract may not be denied legal effect or enforceability solely because an electronic record was used in its formation.

If a law requires a record to be in writing, an electronic record satisfies the law.

If a law requires a signature, an electronic signature satisfies the law.

Effective: August 1, 2000 History: Created 2000 Ky. Acts ch. 301, sec. 7, effective August 1, 2000.

EMS Agency Name: AE062-Bowling Green Patient Name: Marshall, Debbie

Narrative: L: AEL 62 dispatched to Cave City in Kentucky for a scene flight. CEN COM advise the patient weights 80 kg and is a driver of a moped that was hit by a vehicle. The patient to be taken to Tristar Skyline Medical Center for trauma services unavailable at the local area. The patient to be transported via air medical to decrease out of hospital time and to be taken to a higher level of care that the area can provide.

C: Right hip pain with deformity noted.

H: Barren County EMS reports the patient was a driver of a moped with no helmet reported. The patient was rear ended by a vehicle and sent the patient off the moped. No reported loss of consciousness, with a GCS of 15 upon EMS arrival. Upon EMS arrival the patient was placed on a long spine board and a c-collar placed. The patient was undressed and it was noted that there is a deformity and swelling to the right hip. Pulses, motor, sensory intact in all extremities. EMS noted a hematoma to the parietal part of the skull with no bleeding. EMS initiated bilateral 18 gauge IV's, and gave the patient Fentanyl 100 mcg per IV push For pain control. The patient reports she is allergic to Keflex, with a history of depression and hypothyroidism. Medications as as noted in chart. Blood sugar 110 per EMS

A; Primary: No external hemorrhaging noted, airway is patent and self- maintained with equal chest rise and fall, skin warm and dry.

Secondary: GCS 15, RASS 0, Pain3/10. The patient is currently noted in a c-collar and on a long spine board with head blocks placed and secured. There is a hematoma located in the parietal section of the skull with no bleeding noted. Pupils reactive at 2mm. The face presents normal, no blood in the mouth, broken teeth, or swelling. There is a c-collar on place, the neck presents normal with no JVD or tracheal deviation noted. There is a bruise to the left shoulder that is blue in color with abrasion. The right shoulder presents normal. Bilateral lungs sounds are clear with equal chest rise and fall. Heart tone notes S1, S2. The abdomen present soft, non-tender, non-rigid. The pelvis presents stable. The right hip is noted to have swelling and an obvious deformity. The left hip presents normal. There in no bleeding noted to the perineal area. Bilateral extremities are noted to have positive pulse, motor, and sensory. Bilateral upper extremities present with positive pulse, motor, and sensory intact. There are bilateral 18 gauge IV to the antecubital areas that are patent and Free of signs of swelling.

R: Upon arrival to TJ Sampson helipad AEL crew waited approximately 6 minutes For ground crew arrival. Upon arrival the patient was placed on the Zoll monitor including blood pressure, heart rate/rhythm, oxygen saturation, and respiratory rate. The patient declined pain medication at this time with a reported pain level of 3/10. The patient was removed from the rear of the ambulance and placed on AEL cot covered with warm weather blanket and secured with 5 point safety harness. The patient was placed on EMS cot, transported to the aircraft, hot on loaded, and secured via aircraft locking mechanism. The nurse remained with the patient while the paramedic completed safety walk around. Pilot made aware of altitude restrictions and well as the need for the aircraft heater. While en Flight patient temperatures and cabin temperatures were monitored. Continued patient assessment and vitals were monitored during care of AEL crew. Approximately 10 minutes from the receiving Facility radio report was given with trauma alert. All questions answered and no further orders received.

T: Upon landing at the receiving facility and after a 2 minute cool down the patient was off loaded unto the facility stretcher with rails raised For safe transport. AEL crew was escorted to the main desk and then to emergency room 11. AEL equipment was removed From the patient and via multiple lift help the patient was placed on the hospital stretcher. Report was given to Elizabeth RN. The patient GCS remains 15, RASS 0, Pain 3/10. IVs remain intact and patent. Status of the patient remains unchanged.

Ciox Validation Checklist — ROI Standard Requests

Please use the as a checklist when validating your general ROI requests and authorizations.

Patient information, including two identifiers (example: full name, date of birth or social security number).

Name of a provider authorized to release the information.

Name of individual or provider authorized to receive the information.

Specific information to be disclosed/released and re-disclosed /re-released (information contained in the chart may contain records from another facility and were used in the course of treatment of the patient; they may be re-released).

Sensitive information release/non-release. The patient must expressly authorize the release of AIDS/HIV, Drug/Alcohol abuse treatment, mental health, GINA, STDs, etc.

Disclosure / re-disclosure statement. A statement that explains that the patient's health information may no longer be protected by federal privacy regulations once it has been released by the medical facility to the authorized recipient.

Right to revoke statement - The patient has the right to revoke the authorization at a later time provided it has not been acted upon. It must include how to revoke.

Conditions statement — A statement about the ability or inability of the CE to condition treatment, payment, enrollment or eligibility of benefits on whether the individual signs the authorization. | understand that the medical provider to whom this authorization is furnished may not condition its treatment of me on whether or not | sign the authorization.

HCA/Ciox EXCEPTION: Authorizations sent by attorneys and any others who cannot withhold medical treatment are not required to contain the ‘conditioning’ statement.

Purpose of the disclosure statement — Why the patient wants the records to be released.

Authorization expiration: Specific date, event or condition for which consent will expire unless revoked earlier.

Signature of patient or legal Representative (the signature of the patient must be verified by checking the Consent for Treatment/Condition of Admissions form or driver's license).

Date authorization was signed. Check to verify that the authorization is not expired based expiration information above.

4. Use of Biological Samples. During your care at the facility, biological samples (such as blood and tissue samples) might be collected from you for purposes of your care. Sometimes, after your visit there might be excess or leftover biological samples no longer needed for your care. These samples are usually discarded. However, sometimes these samples might be used for research within our hospitals and occasionally made available to researchers at external groups such as universities, private companies, advocacy groups, and government agencies. The research can help answer questions about the causes of diseases, how to prevent them, or even how to treat them. Please note that for this kind of research, (1) there might be no practical way to inform you about the details or results of the research (even if it involves genetic research), (11) generally, no results on tests performed on your samples during the research can be returned to you or entered into your health record, (111) it is not likely that you will directly benefit from the research, and (iv) there are no plans to compensate or recognize you for use of your samples or any discoveries made during the research. When these samples are used in this manner, your privacy is safeguarded consistent with applicable federal and state privacy laws.

If the hospital obtains replacement or reimbursement of cost of your drug or medical product from the manufacturer through such programs, the charge for the product or drug will be removed from your bill. Patient assistance programs require you to sign an application form in order for the hospital to obtain replacement or credits of certain drugs administered or devices implanted to qualifying patients. This LPOA allows the Provider and its claims processor to complete and sign your patient assistance program applications for you for so long as this program may be available to you.

I hereby appoint hospital and/or its claims processor, my attorney-in-fact for the sole and exclusive purpose of signing patient assistance program application forms on my behalf, so that hospital may attempt to obtain replacement or credits of certain drugs administered or devices implanted from the companies that make them. I understand that the final decision as to my acceptance in a patient assistance program lies with each pharmaceutical or medical device company and that submission by hospital provides no guarantee or assurance that any application will be approved. I will provide reasonable assistance and additional information and documentation as necessary to support each application.

Upon return to the Provider by the EBO Servicer, the Provider may place the account back with the EBO Servicer, or, at the option of the Provider, may determine the account to be delinquent, past due and in default.

(C) The Glomerular Filtration Rate is a calculated parameter based on serum Creatinine levels, patient age, and sex. GFR values less than 60 mL/min/1.73 square meters are indicative of Chronic Kidney Disease. Values less than 15 mL/min/1.73 square meters indicate Kidney failure. The calculation for GFR is based on the CKD-EPI(2021) calculation. This formula is race indifferent and is the recommended formula for GFR by the National Kidney Foundation for adults. The GFR will not calculate if the sex is Unknown or if the patient's age is <18 years. We will continue to report a race factor eGFR along with this new result until December 31, 2022.

Important Message from Medicare

Your Rights as a Hospital Inpatient:

You can receive Medicare covered services. This includes medically necessary hospital services and services you may need after you are discharged, if ordered by your doctor. You have a right to know about these services, who will pay for them, and where you can get them.

You can be involved in any decisions about your hospital stay. You can report any concerns you have about the quality of care you receive to your QIO at: KEPRO

1-[PHONE-531] or TTY [PHONE-532]. The QIO is the independent reviewer authorized by Medicare to review the decision to discharge you.

You can work with the hospital to prepare for your safe discharge and arrange for services you may need after you leave the hospital. When you no longer need inpatient hospital care, your doctor or the hospital staff will inform you of your planned discharge date.

You can speak with your doctor or other hospital staff if you have concerns about being discharged.

Your Right to Appeal Your Hospital Discharge:

You have the right to an immediate, independent medical review (appeal) of the decision to discharge you from the hospital. If you do this, you will not have to pay for the services you receive during the appeal (except for charges like copays and deductibles).

If you choose to appeal, the independent reviewer will ask for your opinion. The reviewer also

will look at your medical records and/or other relevant information. You do not have to prepare

anything in writing, but you have the right to do so if you wish.

If you choose to appeal, you and the reviewer will each receive a copy of a detailed explanation about why your covered hospital stay should not continue. You will receive this detailed notice only after you request an appeal.

If the QIO finds that you are not ready to be discharged from the hospital, Medicare will continue to cover your hospital services.

If the QIO agrees services should no longer be covered after the discharge date, neither Medicare nor your Medicare health plan will pay for your hospital stay after noon of the day

after the QIO notifies you of its decision. If you stop services no later than that time, you will avoid financial liability.

If you do not appeal, you may have to pay for any services you receive after your discharge date.

See page 2 of this notice for more information.

Form CMS 10065-IM (Exp. [DOB-577]) OMB approval 0938-1019

Special instructions:

- Create 12/03/22 2225 AKW 12/03/22 2226 AKW 701225 Telemetry Removal NDP A OE Protocol:

<Telemetry Removal NDP Protocol> -- Telemetry Nurse Driven Removal Protocol --

Telemetry with nurse driven removal protocol - telemetry can be

discontinued without an additional MD order if patient no longer meets

criteria for protocol.

TELEMETRY MONITORING INDICATED:

. Significant arrhythmia requiring medical therapy: SVT (supraventricular

achycardia), bradycardia, A. Fib (atrial fibrillation) with RVR (rapid

ventricular response)

2. Acute coronary syndrome or unstable angina with NSTEMI (non-ST elevation

myocardial infarction) or STEMI (ST-elevation myocardial infarction)

3. Pre or post PCI (percutaneous cardiac intervention), CABG (coronary artery bypass with graft), EP (electrophysiology) study, pacemaker or AICD (automatic internal cardiac defibrillator) implantation

4. Medical/surgical patients on IV beta blockers, IV digoxin, ionotropic drips, or other medications requiring close cardiac monitoring (does not include obstetrical patients)

5. Moderate to severe hypokalemia (less than or equal to 3.0) or severe hypomagnesemia (less than or equal to 1.3)

6. Drug or chemical toxicity

7. Suspected pacemaker or AICD malfunction

8. Resuscitated from cardiac arrest or unstable VT (ventricular tachycardia)

9. Syncope of unknown etiology

10. Stroke patients

11. Post vascular procedure

12. Acute decompensated heart failure

13. Sepsis

TELEMETRY NOT INDICATED FOR:

1. Patients who are stable and arrhythmia free for 48 hours of consecutive monitoring and does not meet any criteria in the ‘Telemetry Monitoring Indicated’ list

2. Terminally il] and not a candidate for therapy for arrhythmia

<Urinary Management Protocol Protocol>

--- URINARY MANAGEMENT PROTOCOL --- The Urinary Management Protocol is intended to fully empower nursing to utilize all resources available to them to collect accurate output, with an initial focus on using non-invasive urinary management methods. If followed correctly, this should lead to significant reduction in indwelling urinary catheter (IUC) use.

--- URINARY MANAGEMENT PROTOCOL --- The Urinary Management Protocol is intended to fully empower nursing to utilize all resources available to them to collect accurate output, with an initial focus on using non-invasive urinary management methods. If followed correctly, this should lead to significant reduction in indwelling urinary catheter (IUC) use.

a M<

NOTE: This protocol does not apply to patients who have had urological surgery, indwelling urinary catheters placed by urology, or have a urology consult.

NURSE-DRIVEN FOLEY PROTOCOL (NDFP)

NDFP empowers nursing to remove indwelling urinary catheters (IUC) as soon as they are no longer clinically indicated. Nurses can remove the urinary catheter without a specific order or provider approval.

A. Appropriate indications for maintaining an indwelling urinary catheter include:

Accurate 1&0 and critically il]

Acute retention/obstruction

Assist in skin healing

Gross hematuria/bladder irrigation Palliative care Prolonged immobilization

. Peripartum

B. Assess need of catheter daily.

1. If patient no longer meets indication criteria above for an indwelling urinary catheter and the patient does not have a reason for the catheter to continue, then the catheter will be discontinued. Remove before 12 noon if possible.

SOO WPM

URINARY CATHETER ALGORITHM FOR ACUTE RETENTION AND EARLY REMOVAL (UCARE)

UCARE empowers the nurse to remove the indwelling urinary catheter (TUC) on day 2 of acute urinary retention and assist patient in using active voiding measures as listed below. By removing the IUC after the acute time frame, the current status can be better understood for resolution or continued issues that may need to be further addressed by specialties. While in use, nursing can utilize the in/out (straight) catheter with bladder scan as long as tolerated by the patient. A. Post IUC removal, follow the Urinary Catheter Algorithm for Acute Retention and Early Removal (UCARE): . Encourage active voiding. 2. If not voided in 4-6 hours, scan bladder.

a. If < 180 mL: Assess intake, encourage active voiding, reassess in

Implement appropriate isolation precautions when MRSA positive for A= D prior history or current colonization or infection as follows: OE ~Active MRSA less than 1 year with positive culture and/or active infection : Implement CONTACT PRECAUTIONS ~History of MRSA less than 1 year with no active drainage or other signs of infection: Implement MODIFIED CONTACT PRECAUTIONS ~If known MRSA carrier greater than 1 year with no positive cultures: A =>) Follow STANDARD PRECAUTIONS OE 2. Concurrently begin: ~Daily chlorhexidine (CHG) bathing for 5 consecutive days or longer if patient has central venous access device or in ICU ~Mupirocin or iodophor to nares twice daily for 5 consecutive days 3. Decolonization criteria: ~All patients in Intensive care unit, patients identified as high isk on the first point of contact screen, patients known to be MRSA positive by prior history or new positive lab results

~Use an alternative for patients with known allergy to mupirocin or iodine ~Continue mupirocin/iodophor nasal product and CHG treatment if

transferred to another level of care to complete 5 full consecutive

days ~Apply product to anterior nares for 30 seconds each side (slowly

clockwise for count of 5, counter clockwise for count of 5)

DISCONTINUE CONTACT PRECAUTIONS FOR MRSA: - After off all anti-MRSA antibiotics and completing the decolonization protocol for 5 full consecutive days:

1. Wait for 48-72 hours after completion

Protocol: <Rapid Response Protocol Protocol> *%* Rapid Response Protocol *** A. Nursing Orders: (All patients) Insert peripheral IV if No patent IV access Establish and maintain the patient's airway Continuous cardiac monitoring place on bedside monitor Initiate Oxygen Therapy Protocol * Oxygen Therapy: Only start on Oxygen therapy if SpO02 is less than

than 90% * Device: asal Cannula * Rate: 1 Liter per minute 2 L/Min

* Initiate 02 Therapy Protocol: Yes No

* Tnitiate 02 weaning protocol: Yes No

* Titrate to Maintain Sp02: 90-96%

if greater than 51 nasal cannula required change to face mask starting at 40% Fi02 and Notify provider.

Suction Airway as needed

Notify attending physician of change in patient status and interventions performed.

Fingerstick blood glucose now

Give 25 milliliters of D50 if blood glucose below 80

Give 50 milliliters of D50 if blood glucose below 60

B. Cardiac Clinical Changes:

Heart Rate less than 40 (symptomatic)

1.) Atropine 1 milligram intravenous push now per ACLS protocol Heart Rate greater than 180 (symptomatic)

1.) 12 Lead EKG Now Chest Pain 1.) EKG Now and give to a provider within 10 minutes - may give to ED provider or in-house provider. 2.) Aspirin 81 milligrams orally x 4 chewed and swallow if no allergies, active bleeding, warfarin use, or unless taken within the last 24 hours 3.) Nitroglycerin 0.4 milligrams sublingual, may repeat every 5 minutes x2 doses if systolic BP greater than 90

4.) Troponin stat 5.) Upon identification of ST-Elevation initiate the STEMI process. Call hospital operator to page out Stemi Alert.

Systolic Blood Pressure less than 90 (symptomatic)

1.) Normal saline 250 milliliters intravenous bolus if no crackles, rhonchi or complaints of dyspnea; may repeat x 1

C. Respiratory Allergy and Anaphylaxis:

STAT Portable Chest x-ray (obtain if an acute respiratory distress problem). Administer nebulized Albuterol 2.5 mg (unless patient is presently on a nebulizer treatment protocol) in 3 mL saline. Arterial Blood Gas per Respiratory Therapy if unable to improve saturation with oxygen therapy and or suspected C02 retention.

If BiPap required, initiate with the following settings, inspiratory pressure of 12 cm H20, expiratory pressure of 6cm H20, titrating as indicated Patient assessment of crackles/rhonchi and patient complaint of dyspnea 1.) administer furosemide (Lasix) 20 milligrams intravenous now. 2.) Decrease/Discontinue IV fluids

K. Altered Level of consciousness or change in mental status post narcotic administration:

Naloxone (Narcan) 0.2 milligrams IV push now if recent narcotic administered and any of the following are present:

1.) Decreased level of consciousness

2.) Pinpoint pupils (less than 3 mm)

3.) Respiratory rate less than 8/min

May repeat naloxone (Narcan) 0.2 milligrams intravenous push after 5 minutes to a maximum of 0.4 milligrams total

L. Altered Level of consciousness or change in mental status post benzodiazepine administration: Flumazenil (Romazicon) 0.2 milligrams intravenous push now if recent Benzodiazepine administered and any of the following are present:

1.) Decreased level of consciousness

2.) Respiratory rate less than 8/min

May repeat flumazenil (Romazicon) 0.2 milligrams intravenous push every 1 minute to a maximum of 1 milligram total.

Protocol: <Oxygen Therapy Protocol> -- Oxygen Therapy Protocol: Adult --

INITIATION:

A. Supplemental oxygen will occur after verification of a provider's order, starting at the rate specified in the order.

a. The oxygen liter flow will be adjusted in 1-liter increments in order to achieve and maintain specific oxygen saturation (Sp02) target

range specified in provider order.

B. Patients will be placed on oxygen to maintain an oxygen saturation poe) parget range. Exception: COPD patients, keep Sp02 between 88-92% (unless otherwise ordered) b. Exception: Acute stroke patients, keep Sp02 greater than 94% (unless otherwise ordered) C. A nasal cannula is indicated unless unable to maintain the ordered Sp02 target range. 1. Liter flow not to exceed 6 liters/minute (LPM) 2. Assess patient need for continuous pulse oximetry when receiving greater than or equal to 5 LPM 02 per nasal cannula or Fi02 greater than 40% D. If the patient’s Sp02 goal cannot be achieved with the use of a nasal cannula, the respiratory therapist (RT) should be notified and the RT

ay step a patient up to the next oxygen delivery device titrated to the owest level of oxygen needed to maintain target Sp02 range. Notify provider with each device change. If unable to maintain target Sp02, notify provider immediately for orders. Call Rapid Response if provider not immediately available.

. Simple mask

Venturi mask

OxyMask

Partial/non-rebreathing mask

High flow oxygen

OB WP

ONITORING:

A. Adult patients included in the oxygen therapy protocol will receive oxygen saturation assessments and titration, if indicated, per guidelines for modification of oxygen therapy. RT to assess and escalate therapy as indicated.

B. If patient is in distress, contact physician immediately and do not leave patient unattended.

C. ABG Indications:

1. If unable to obtain Sp02, a provider should be notified and an ABG ABG ordered for hemodynamic status.

2. If there are concerns for the patient's oxygenation or acid-base status (e.g. increase in confusion/disorientation, diaphoresis, use

of accessory muscles, tachycardia, tachypnea, tachypnea, cyanosis),

a provider should be notified and an ABG ordered.

<End of Protocol>

-- Oxygen Weaning Protocol: Adult --

MODIFICATION GUIDELINES:

A. Notify patient’s nurse of all oxygen titrations if completed by RT. B. All titrations must be appropriately documented.

C. Once patient is within ordered target Sp02 range and vital signs are stable per vital sign parameter order, proceed to weaning:

. Simple face mask patients who require liter flow less than 6 LPM will need to be switched to a nasal cannula starting with a flow rate of less than 5 LPM. 2. For patients on blended oxygen, the Fi02 will be managed by RT in increments of 10% while maintaining the target Sp02 range from order. 3. RT to convert to nasal cannula when Fi02 is less than 40%.

4. Nasal cannula titration will begin with decrease in liter flow by 1 LPM, to lowest liter flow needed to maintain target Sp02 range.

5. If tolerated, continue to wean oxygen to room air, using discontinuation guidelines. a. Oxygen therapy should not be discontinued/weaned for patients with

a documented history of chronic hypoxemia (e.g. COPD) that wear

oxygen at home unless otherwise ordered by physician.

D. If patient unable to maintain target Sp02, discontinue weaning and follow Oxygen Therapy Protocol. Maintain the lowest Fi02/liter flow required to keep Sp02 at target range.

E. Notify physician if patient is not able to wean for home 02 evaluation order.

DISCONTINUATION GUIDELINES:

A. Once patient is on 1 LPM or less, place on room air.

1. Check patient’s Sp02 within 1 hour of placing on room air and then per vital sign order unless otherwise indicated, with proper documentation. 2. Communicate discontinuation of 02 therapy to appropriate healthcare professionals. B. If Sp02 less than ordered target range, resume 02 therapy and follow Oxygen Therapy Protocol. <End of Protocol>

- Obtain MRSA nares screening swab on ALL admissions for the following criteria, if none of the listed criteria is met Nursing may cancel the swab order:

1. Prior MRSA history in Meditech - located within First Point of Contact screen or Health History

Active MRSA less than 1 year with positive culture and/or active infection: Implement CONTACT PRECAUTIONS

History of MRSA less than 1 year with no active drainage or other

signs of infection: Implement MODIFIED CONTACT PRECAUTIONS

If known MRSA carrier greater than 1 year with no positive cultures: Follow STANDARD PRECAUTIONS

2. First Point of Contact NUR inpatient admission/transfer queries for high risk: Nursing home Long term care facility Other healthcare facility Other hospital Jail/prison Homeless shelter

End stage renal dialysis care

Surgical procedure: Open heart, spine, or joint replacement

Known IV Drug User and/or draining wounds

3. Nasal swab should be taken from anterior nares, not deep

-If applicable, primary site (e.g. wound) should also be swabbed

4. Only swab patient’s nares who have been off anti-MRSA antibiotics for at least 48 hours

DECOLONIZATION:

- Targeted decolonization for NON-ICU if MRSA nares screening swab is POSITIVE, prior history of MRSA within 1 year OR patient is identified as high risk based on first point of contact screening. - Universal decolonization for ALL adult and pediatric ICU patients 1. Implement appropriate isolation precautions when MRSA positive for prior history or current colonization or infection as follows:

Active MRSA less than 1 year with positive culture and/or active infection : Implement CONTACT PRECAUTIONS History of MRSA less than 1 year with no active drainage or other signs of infection: Implement MODIFIED CONTACT PRECAUTIONS

If known MRSA carrier greater than 1 year with no positive cultures: Follow STANDARD PRECAUTIONS 2. Concurrently begin: Daily chlorhexidine (CHG) bathing for 5 consecutive days or longer if patient has central venous access device or in ICU

upirocin or iodophor to nares twice daily for 5 consecutive days

3. Decolonization criteria:

All patients in Intensive care unit, patients identified as high

risk on the first point of contact screen, patients known to be

RSA positive by prior history or new positive lab results

Use an alternative for patients with known allergy to mupirocin or jodine Continue mupirocin/iodophor nasal product and CHG treatment if transferred to another level of care to complete 5 full consecutive days Apply product to anterior nares for 30 seconds each side (slowly clockwise for count of 5, counter clockwise for count of 5)

DISCONTINUE CONTACT PRECAUTIONS FOR MRSA: - After off all anti-MRSA antibiotics and completing the decolonization protocol for 5 full consecutive days:

Protocol: <Urinary Management Protocol Protocol> --- URINARY MANAGEMENT PROTOCOL --- The Urinary Management Protocol is intended to fully empower nursing to utilize all resources available to them to collect accurate output, with an initial focus on using non-invasive urinary management methods. If followed correctly, this should lead to significant reduction in indwelling urinary catheter (IUC) use.

NOTE: This protocol does not apply to patients who have had urological surgery, indwelling urinary catheters placed by urology, or have a urology consult.

PRE-CATHETER AVOIDANCE REVIEW AND EXCLUSION (P-CARE)

On admission, evaluate ability to capture urinary output using the processes below. - If IUC is ordered, complete 2-person attestation w/ approval prior to insertion * TUCs can be approved up to first 48 hours then reviewed daily for: “Critical 1&0 requiring hourly reads

CBI w/ active hematuria GU surgery Proning > 12 hours on paralytics Sedated AND paralyzed

NURSE-DRIVEN FOLEY PROTOCOL (NDFP)

NDFP empowers nursing to remove indwelling urinary catheters (IUC) as soon as they are no longer clinically indicated. Nurses can remove the urinary catheter without a specific order or provider approval.

A. Appropriate indications for maintaining an indwelling urinary catheter include: 1. Accurate 180 and critically il] 2. Acute retention/obstruction

<Telemetry Removal NDP Protocol> -- Telemetry Nurse Driven Removal Protocol --

Protocol:

Telemetry with nurse driven removal protocol - telemetry can be discontinued without an additional MD order if patient no longer meets criteria for protocol.

TELEMETRY MONITORING INDICATED:

. Significant arrhythmia requiring medical therapy: SVT (supraventricular tachycardia), bradycardia, A. Fib (atrial fibrillation) with RVR (rapid ventricular response)

2. Acute coronary syndrome or unstable angina with NSTEMI (non-ST elevation myocardial infarction) or STEMI (ST-elevation myocardial infarction)

. Pre or post PCI (percutaneous cardiac intervention), CABG (coronary artery bypass with graft), EP (electrophysiology) study, pacemaker or

AICD (automatic internal cardiac defibrillator) implantation

4. Medical/surgical patients on IV beta blockers, IV digoxin, ionotropic drips, or other medications requiring close cardiac monitoring (does not include obstetrical patients)

5. Moderate to severe hypokalemia (less than or equal to 3.0) or severe hypomagnesemia (less than or equal to 1.3)

6. Drug or chemical toxicity

7. Suspected pacemaker or AICD malfunction

8. Resuscitated from cardiac arrest or unstable VT (ventricular tachycardia)

9. Syncope of unknown etiology

0. Stroke patients

1. Post vascular procedure

2. Acute decompensated heart failure

3. Sepsis

ELEMETRY NOT INDICATED FOR:

. Patients who are stable and arrhythmia free for 48 hours of consecutive onitoring and does not meet any criteria in the ‘Telemetry Monitoring ndicated’ list il] and not

2. Terminally medications, comfort care patients

a candidate for therapy for arrhythmia

3. Patients with chronic, rate controlled, stable A. Fib 4. Patients with asymptomatic PVCs (premature ventricular contractions) not hospitalized for cardiac reasons <End of Protocol> Order’s Audit Trail of Events

Interpretive Data #1: T4 Free Thyroid hormone autoantibodies in serum samples may cause interference in immunoassays.

Heterophilic antibodies in serum or plasma samples may cause interference in immunoassyas. These anitbodies may be present in blood samples from individuals regularly exposed to animals who have been treated with animal serum products.

Some drugs and some nonthyroidal patient conditions are known to alter Free T4 concentrations in vivo. When interpreting FT4 results, note the potential effects of certain drugs on the free-hormone equilibrium.

369.107 Legal recognition of electronic records, electronic signatures, and electronic contracts, (1) Avrecord or signature may not be denied legal effect or enforceability solely because it is in electronic form, (2) A contract may not be denied legal effect or enforceability solely because an electronic record was used in its formation, (3) Ifa law requires a record to be in writing, an electronic record satisfies the law, (4) Ifa law requires a signature, an electronic signature satisfies the law. Effective: August 1, 2000 History: Created 2000 Ky. Acts ch, 301, sec. 7, ofiactive August 1, 2000,

Moreover, | have the right to ask questions and discuss my concerns with my healthcare provider.

A. HIV/Hepatitis Testing. | understand that HIV (human immunodeficiency virus)/AIDS, Hepatitis C and Hepatitis B tests may be performed on me without my consent if a health professional, facility employee or first responder sustains an exposure to my blood or other body fluid. | further understand that my blood will NOT be routinely tested for these diseases unless ordered by my provider and that the results of any testing will be kept confidential.

B. Photographic Consent. | hereby consent that photographs may be taken of me/the patient for clinical purpose. This consent is strictly giving permission for TJ Regional Health to take all necessary photographs needed before and after any treatment/procedure and/or to be used for the purpose of monitoring my progress in the clinic. | understand the photographs taken will become a part of my/the patient medical record.

Release of Medical Information. | understand that both electronic and paper-based documentation of medical

care received are maintained. This medical or health record typically includes information about my/the

patient’s symptoms and health condition; results of physical examinations and diagnostic tests; a plan regarding future care and treatment; as well as demographic and photographic identifiers. Such individually identifiable information about me/the patient is protected health information and, as such, will be used, shared, or disclosed only for the purpose of treatment, payment, and healthcare operations or as required by law.

Otherwise, it will not be inspected or released without my specific authorization except in certain circumstances

as outline in the Notice of Privacy Practices (available upon request).

A. Health Information Exchange Notification. Health Information Exchange (HIE) is a way for health care providers, hospital, laboratories, and organizations involved in your care coordination and payment to see your electronic health records remotely via a secure network to provide you with the appropriate medical treatment and related services. | hereby authorize TJ Regional Health to share my health information to the HIE. | understand this will remain in effect from the date of my signature below and applies to information in existence as of this date and any additional health information that may come into existence. The health care organization(s) and HIE will use this information for the purpose of continuity of your/the patient's care and will maintain the information according to its own policies and practices. It may re-disclose some or all of that information as permitted by state and federal laws and regulations.

Financial Agreement.

History of Present Illness

Previously seen by Dr. Koury for memory loss, concussion, and headaches. Past medical history of hypothyroidism, depression.

Patient states that after a motor vehicle accident ( hit by car while on a scooter) in December 2022, patient had new onset memory loss, difficulty talking, and head pain.

Patient states she had difficulty concentrating and increased forgetfulness since the accident. Previous work-up by Dr. Koury for reversible dementia etiologies, was negative. Patient states that has been steadily improving. At the time of the accident, she was told that she had a subdural hematoma. She denies loss of consciousness with the event, but reports hitting her head on the ground. She is an ongoing legal litigation regarding this manner.

Patient states that she is having head pain which is a sharp 1 second pain in different areas of the head including the front, back left, and right temple. These pains are 10/10 but last only for 1 second. She reports history of migraine, and denies that this is similar to previous migraines. She does not want any medications for this at this time.

Reviewed diagnostics: - MRI brain without contrast: Minimal white matter disease, consistent for age and history, likely secondary to hypertension - MRA head without contrast: Normal - MRI cervical spine without contrast: Mild DDD, severe right cervical 3-4, 4-5 neuroforaminal stenosis Physical Exam Vitals & Measurements T: 36.8 °C (Temporal Artery) HR: 76 (Peripheral) RR: 20 BP: *:202/84 SpO2: 99% HT: 170.18 cm WT: 74.57 kg BMI: 25.75 BSA: 1.88 General: No acute distress, Well developed/groomed/nourished ENT: Oropharhynx without any erythema or exudate. 2/21/1956 * Auth (Verified) * Person Full Name: MARSHALL, DEBRA] FAY Regional Health GENERAL CONSENT TO seo OUTPATIENT TREATMENT = fin one T7Samson Tf Health Columbia Consent to Clinic and Associated Outpatient Services |, amit pate: 5/25/2023

1. Consent for Treatment. | authorize and consent to TJ Regional Health providers and their staff for care, treatment, and testing performed at TJ Regional Health. This is to include, physical examinations, diagnostic imaging procedures (such as x-rays, CT scans, ultrasounds, mammograms, and/or magnetic resonance imaging (MRi)}), laboratory tests, and other non-invasive diagnostic and therapeutic procedures and/or treatments including wound care and rehabilitation services, as my/the patient’s provider considers to be necessary or appropriate for the purpose of diagnostic and/or treatment of my/the patient’s condition. | do understand that \/the patient have the right to refuse to consent to any proposed care, testing, or treatment: Moreover, | have the right to ask questions and discuss my concerns with my healthcare provider.

A. HIV/Hepatitis Testing. | understand that HIV (human immunodeficiency virus)/AIDS, Hepatitis C and Hepatitis B tests may be performed on me without my consent if a health professional, facility employee or first responder sustains an exposure to my blood or other body fluid. | further understand that my blood will NOT be routinely tested for these diseases unless ordered by my provider and that the results of any testing will be kept confidential.

B. Photographic Consent. | hereby consent that photographs may be taken of me/the patient for clinical purpose. This consent is strictly giving permission for TJ Regional Health to take all necessary photographs needed before and after any treatment/procedure and/or to be used for the purpose of monitoring my progress in the clinic. | understand the photographs taken will become a part of my/the patient medical record.

2. Release of Medical information. | understand that both electronic and paper-based documentation of medical care received are maintained. This medical or health record typically includes information about my/the patient’s symptoms and health condition; results of physical examinations and diagnostic tests; a plan regarding future care and treatment; as well as demographic and photographic identifiers. Such individually identifiable information about me/the patient is protected health information and, as such, will be used, shared, or disclosed only for the purpose of treatment, payment, and healthcare operations or as required by law. Otherwise, it will not be inspected or released without my specific authorization except in certain circumstances as outline in the Notice of Privacy Practices (available upon request).

A. Health information Exchange Notification. Health Information Exchange (HIE) is a way for health care providers, hospital, laboratories, and organizations involved in your care coordination and payment to see your electronic health records remotely via a secure network to provide you with the appropriate medical treatment and related services. | hereby authorize TJ Regional Health to share my health information to the HIE. | understand this will remain in effect from the date of my signature below and applies to information in existence as of this date and any additional health information that may come into existence. The health care organization(s) and HIE will use this information for the purpose of continuity of your/the patient’s care and will maintain the information according to its own policies and practices. It may re-disclose some or all of that information as permitted by state and federal laws and regulations.

IV Contrast Statement: Some examinations require the administration of a contrast agent, which will make tissues, organs and pathologies visible on the MRI images. This contrast contains no Iodine or radioactivity. The contrast is injected into a vein in the arm or hand and circulates throughout the body allowing us to visualize the difference between various tissues and organs as well as abnormalities, which might not be seen otherwise. The use of contrast will aide the radiologist in interpreting your examination as well as aiding your physician in diagnosing your case and planning any treatment, that may be necessary. While the risk of a reaction to the contrast is very low, but as with any medication risks are involved. Reactions can vary from simple nausea to death. We are prepared to treat any reaction that could occur, If you understand and accept these risks for contrast and items on the Jist above, please sign below. Radiology Report Exam: MRI cervical spine.

HISTORY: Back pain.

FINDINGS: MR imaging of the cervical spine in the sagittal, axial, and coronal planes using multiple Limited seems is on 8/14/2023 compared with the previous of 9/11/2017.

The bone marrow signal is normal. There is grade 1 degenerative anterolisthesis of C5 on C6 measuring 1 mm related to prominent facet arthropathy which is noted from C2 through C6. There is no facet edema. There is disc dehydration diffusely.

There is endplate sclerosis and spurring from C3 through 7. There is no soft tissue inflammation or fluid collection. The spinal cord is normal in signal and contour. Level specific detail follow.

At C2-3, the spinal canal and neural foramen are widely patent.

C3-4, there is minimal ventral thecal impression from uncovertebral hypertrophy. Hypertrophic changes cause severe right and mild left foraminal stenosis.

At C4-5, there is minimal ventral thecal impression from uncovertebral hypertrophy. There is prominent right and no left foraminal stenosis.

At C5-6, there is minimal ventral thecal impression from uncovertebral hypertrophy. The foramen are widely patent.

At C6-7, there is minimal ventral thecal impression from uncovertebral hypertrophy. The foramen are widely patent.

And C7-T1, the spinal canal and neural foramen are widely patent.

IMPRESSION:

1. Mild degenerative disc change with endplate sclerosis as detailed above. There is prominent secondary right foraminal stenosis at C3-4 and C4-5.

2. Prominent diffuse facet arthropathy without facet edema.

A. HIV/Hepatitis Testing. | understand that HIV (human immunodeficiency virus)/AIDS, Hepatitis C and Hepatitis B tests may be performed on me without my consent if a health professional, facility employee or first responder sustains an exposure to my blood or other body fluid. | further understand that my blood will NOT be routinely tested for these diseases unless ordered by my provider and that the results of any testing will be kept confidential.

Release of Medical Information: | understand that both electronic and paper-based documentation of medical

care received are maintained. This medical or health record typically includes information about my/the

patient’s symptoms and health condition; results of physical examinations and diagnostic tests; a plan regarding future care and treatment; as well as demographic and photographic identifiers. Such individually identifiable information about me/the patient is protected health information and, as such, will be used, shared, or disclosed only for the purpose of treatment, payment, and healthcare operations or as required by law.

Otherwise, it will not be inspected or released without my specific authorization except in certain circumstances

as outline in the Notice of Privacy Practices (available upon request).

A. Health Information Exchange Notification. Health Information Exchange (HIE) is a way for health care providers, hospital, laboratories, and organizations involved in your care coordination and payment to see your electronic health records remotely via a secure network to provide you with the appropriate medical treatment and related services. | hereby authorize TJ Regional Health to share my health information to the HIE. | understand this will remain in effect from the date of my signature below and applies to information in existence as of this date and any additional health information that may come into existence. The health care organization(s) and HIE will use this information for the purpose of continuity of your/the patient’s care and will maintain the information according to its own policies and practices. It may re-disclose some or all of that information as permitted by state and federal! laws and regulations.

HIPAA COMPLIANT MEDICAL AUTHORIZATION

(Authorization to Release Protected Health Care Information)

To: Air Evac EMS Inc — Prestonburg P.O. Box 106 West Plains, MO 65775

Dear Medical Records Clerk:

I have retained The Whaley Law Firm, PSC to represent me in matters related to an injury sustained due to a third parties’ negligence. Please forward a copy of any & all records not previously provided to The Whaley Law Firm upon request.

Pursuant to the Health Insurance Portability & Accountability Act (HIPAA) Privacy Regulations, 45 CFR 164.508, the provider listed above is hereby authorized to release to The Whaley Law Firm, PSC or any of their representatives, all medical records, including but not limited to: Office Notes, History, Physical, Consultation Notes, Discharge Summaries, Orders, Progress Notes, Laboratory Results, Nurses’ Notes, Emergency Room Records, Operative Reports, In-Patient Records and films of X-Rays, MRIs, CT Scans, or PET Scans, Pharmacy and Drug Records, Medical Bills and Health Insurance Information, Medicaid/Medicare Records, concerning ANY medical treatment that I have received from you and/or at your facility, as well as ALL such records which you keep in the regular course of business that are found in my medical record file.

I hereby authorize the release of ANY & ALL records regarding mental health, psychiatric (other than psychotherapy notes, which must be requested under separate authorization), Chemical Dependency or HIV.

A photostatic copy hereof shall be as valid as the original.

Thereby authorize a FREE COPY of my medical records pursuant to KRS 422.317 be sent to the extent [ have not already requested my one free copy.

The purpose of this authorization and request is to permit my attorney to obtain ALL medical information pertaining to my physical and mental condition(s). This authorization expires in three (3) years trom the date of the signature. The aforementioned expiration date has not passed, as this matter is on-going. I hereby authorize The Whaley Law Firm, PSC. to speak to my healthcare providers privately or to take the testimony at deposition and/or trial as may be requested.

Ihave the right to revoke this authorization in writing by providing a signed, written notice of revocation to the healthcare provider listed above and to The Whaley Law Firm, PSC. I understand that there are exceptions to the right to revoke. Among the exceptions to the right to revoke are that an individual may not revoke an authorization to the extent that the covered entity has taken action in reliance thereon. Medical Providers

may not condition treatment or payment on whether the above-listed patient executes this authorization. The information disclosed pursuant to this authorization may be subject to re-disclosure and no longer protected by the privacy regulations promulgated pursuant to the Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act (HIPAA)

369.107 Legal recognition of electronic records, electronic signatures, and

(1) (2)

(3) (4)

electronic contracts.

A record or signature may not be denied legal effect or enforceability solely because it is in electronic form. A contract may not be denied legal effect or enforceability solely because an electronic record was used in its formation. If a law requires a record to be in writing, an electronic record satisfies the law. If a law requires a signature, an electronic signature satisfies the law.

Effective: August 1, 2000

History: Created 2000 Ky. Acts ch. 301, sec. 7, effective August 1, 2000.
